</span><strong><span>link graph matrix</span></strong><span> </span><span class="MathJax_SVG" tabindex="-1" style="font-size: 100%; display: inline-block;"><svg xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" width="1.582ex" height="2.066ex" viewBox="0 -783.2 681 889.4" role="img" focusable="false" style="vertical-align: -0.247ex;"><defs><path stroke-width="0" id="E41-MJMATHI-4C" d="M228 637Q194 637 192 641Q191 643 191 649Q191 673 202 682Q204 683 217 683Q271 680 344 680Q485 680 506 683H518Q524 677 524 674T522 656Q517 641 513 637H475Q406 636 394 628Q387 624 4 553 3T537 0T494 -1Q483 -1 418 -1T294 0H116Q32 0 32 10Q32 17 34 24Q39 43 44 45Q48 46 59 46H65Q92 46 125 49Q139 52 144 61Q147 65 216 339T285 628Q285 635 228 637Z"></path></defs><g stroke="currentColor" fill="currentColor" stroke-width="0" transform="matrix(1 0 0 -1 0 0)"><use xlink:href="#E41-MJMATHI-4C" x="0" y="0"></use></g></svg></span><script type="math/tex">L</script><span> is found from the adjacency matrix by normalizing (each column) with respect to the number of outlinks so each column sums to unity. </span><a href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PageRank#Algebraic'><span>Google&#39;s Page Rank Algorithm</span></a></p></blockquote><blockquote><p><span>Example: a simple linear operation </span></p><p><span>	</span><span>Consider a polygon </span><span class="MathJax_SVG" tabindex="-1" style="font-size: 100%; display: inline-block;"><svg xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circulant_matrix'><span>Circulant</span></a><span>: each row is a shifted (circularly to the right by one column) version of the previous orw.</span></p><p><span>Always square in this class.</span></p><p><span>Arises when considering periodic boundary conditions, </span><span class="MathJax_SVG" tabindex="-1" style="font-size: 100%;
